Grain

The New Rice Market is Declining

Yesterday, the number of ships arriving at Zhabei Luli Road was around 40, mainly carrying new rice. Sales on this street were sluggish and there were few transactions, and market sentiment was very weak. Fortunately, the price of broken rice stabilized because the river inventory of this product was less than 200 shi, so the price was still set at 20.078 yuan. There was a surge in deliveries of Western new rice, with 20 ships arriving yesterday. Buying interest was very weak, and prices continued to fall sharply. The opening price in the morning was still at 19.23 yuan, but the best quality goods were only at 19 to 18.8 yuan in the afternoon, a drop of 1.1 yuan from the previous day. It is difficult for this kind of declining market to stabilize, and most people expect it to fall to 16 or 17 yuan. The arrival of Eastern new rice was still not significant, but it was difficult to maintain the inventory, so selling pressure increased, and the price fell by another half yuan. Currently, the opening price is 19 to 18.5 yuan, and ordinary rice is already around 18 yuan. Deliveries of new Yangjian rice were also eager, and outbound sales were sluggish. Observations showed that goods priced at 13.5 yuan were already of upper-middle quality, so goods priced at 14 yuan must be particularly high quality. However, given this market situation, it is necessary to see a short decline of 4 to 6 coppers. New Dujian, New Suibaijian, New Bujian, etc. also fell sharply across the board, dropping by 2, 3, 4, or 5 coppers, and it was difficult to stop the decline. Only New Kejian saw a slight rise of 1 or 2 coppers because the shorts were covering their positions due to the continuous sharp declines. High-quality goods were priced at 13 yuan, and ordinary goods at 12.5 yuan. Currently, the market for New Rice and Geng Youmi is not easy to maintain. The owners of the arriving Shanghai goods are all seeking quick sales, because the next batch will arrive soon, so they are competing to sell first. Therefore, the market situation still needs to be downstream. The arrival of goods at Yuanhe was slight, and sales were flat. The price was still above the 19 yuan mark.

Yesterday, about 10 ships arrived in Hunan, Shanghai. The market situation was weak. High-quality old broken rice was exhausted. There was little trading in the mid-level passes, and prices were tired by half copper. The opening price was 19.5 yuan. The market shape of thin broken rice was flat and tired, but there was little going in and out due to the lack of goods. New rice also fell here, and high-quality goods opened at only 18.5 yuan, needing to subtract 4 to 5 coppers. Deliveries of Xiang rice were few, and the price was slightly short by two coppers. The price was reluctantly opened at 19.78 yuan. New Yangjian saw a drop of 3 to 4 coppers, with high-quality rice at 13.5 yuan. Dujian was the same, while Baijian opened at 15.5 yuan, only recovering 2 coppers. The decline here felt slightly more peaceful, but the market followed the northern market.

Sugar Market

Wufu Ice Industry Has Sold Out

Although the ice business has been active recently, customers are focusing on top-quality products. The two batches of Wufu ice that arrived were immediately sold out. Yesterday, 150 boxes were opened, with each box priced at 6 taels and 7 qian. This batch has been completely sold out. According to telegraphic reports, the factory is rushing to produce more, and it is expected to arrive soon. In addition, the quality of Wangmao ice has been improving recently. Yesterday, several hundred boxes were opened, priced at 6 taels and 6 qian, on par with Wufu ice. It has promising prospects.

North-South Goods

Xinghua Grade Two Appears

New Xinghua Grade Two Longans arrived yesterday on three ships from Fu'an and other places. The total number of boxes exported from the production area reached 27,000, with about 10,000 boxes shipped to Shanghai. The rest were transferred to Ningbo and other places for sale. This year's Xing Yuan harvest is quite abundant. It is expected that the standard Jiechun Grade Two will be around 50 taels. The evening meeting decided that formal sales will begin today.

Silk and Tea

Shaoxing Autumn Cocoon Market Ends

A Little Over 30% of the Cocoons are Spun; Cocoon Prices are 56 Yuan per Spindle

This year's autumn cocoon harvest in the four townships of Shaoxing was poor, and only 40% of the cocoon shops opened. After six or seven days of opening, there were very few goods arriving on the market, and the cocoon market ended. Only a little over 30% of the cocoons are spun, and the amount received by the cocoon shops is limited. Also, there are not many high-quality cocoons, and the average cocoon price is 56 yuan per spindle. A portion of the officials responsible for handling the autumn cocoons have already returned to Shanghai.

Local News

Yesterday's Memorial Service for

Mr. Zhu Zhixin

Attended by Over 400 Representatives

Yesterday was the tenth anniversary of the martyrdom of Mr. Zhu Zhixin, a martyr of our party. The Propaganda Department of the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Committee specially organized a memorial service at the Republican Theater on Minguo Road in the southern city at 9:00 am. All party departments, agencies, and groups at all levels in the city were notified in advance to send four representatives to participate. More than 400 representatives attended. The meeting was presided over by Yang Qingyuan, Minister of the Municipal Propaganda Department, who reported on Mr. Zhu Zhixin's revolutionary history and the efforts we should make. Tao Baichuan and others then gave speeches. The details are recorded below:

Order of the Meeting

1. All stand at attention. 2. Sing the party song. 3. Pay the highest respect to the party's national flag, the portrait of the Prime Minister, and the portrait of Mr. Zhu Zhixin. 4. The chairman respectfully reads the Prime Minister's will. 5. Observe silence. 6. The chairman reports. 7. Speeches. 8. Shout slogans. 9. Adjournment.

Meeting Staff

Chairman: Yang Qingyuan; Recorder: Zhou Hanmei; Master of Ceremonies: Xu Yefu; Reception: Chen Yunhuang, Li Bingjun, Zhang Hongwei, Peng Yongjie; Secretaries: Cao Huaqiu, Hong Dichun, Zhang Hanbao, Jiang Zhenwu

Participating Groups

Municipal Government: Chen Kecheng, Zhou Rong; Municipal Education Bureau: Zhang Yanggao; Municipal Finance Bureau: Gan Zongdao, Cai Wenchuan, Sun Changduo, Zhou Yizhong; Municipal Social Affairs Bureau: Shen Zuxin; Land Bureau: Qiu Yunming, Shao Guangzu; Port Bureau: Zhou Yuanhua, Sun Changheng; Public Works Bureau: Jiang Sanhua; Public Utilities Bureau: Zhao Qingyang; Public Security Bureau: Zhang Tao, He Shiming; Health Bureau: Li Ping, Wu Zhaofan, Wu Pengling; China National Products Maintenance Association: Xu Genghua; Shanghai Local Court: Wang Xun; Special District Local Court: Yu Ding; Shanghai Citizens' National Products Promotion Association: Shen Shuyu; Women's Association: Lin Kecong; as well as party departments at all levels, trade unions, group union secretaries' training institutes, all students, etc., totaling more than 400 people.

Chairman's Report

Fellow comrades, representatives from all walks of life: Today is the tenth anniversary of the martyrdom of Mr. Zhu Zhixin. We commemorate the day ten years ago in the Republic of China when Mr. Zhu Zhixin, a martyr of our party, a believer of the Prime Minister, and the creator and protector of the Republic of China, was murdered by the Gui系 warlords. Mr. Zhu's sacrifice for the country and the nation is certainly worthy of our commemoration. His daily actions, scholarship, and morality are also worthy of our enthusiastic commemoration. Mr. Zhu was exceptionally intelligent. He received excellent teaching from his father in his childhood. Therefore, at the age of sixteen, he had a deep understanding of Chinese classics such as the Four Books and Five Classics, the Twenty-Four Histories, and was knowledgeable about all scientific common sense. After the age of sixteen, he studied mathematics because he felt that mathematics was the foundation of all sciences. Therefore, he was proficient in algebra and calculus. After the age of twenty, he studied politics and law in Japan. Therefore, Mr. Zhu also had a profound understanding of social sciences. After returning to China, he studied English and Russian. Thanks to his extraordinary intelligence and diligent study, he was fluent in difficult texts of any country. This is Mr. Zhu's educational experience. Later, when he entered society, he devoted himself to revolution. He worked even harder in promoting the revolution through writing, helping to organize the Chinese Revolutionary Party in Japan, calling on comrades to found the Min Bao newspaper, publicizing the true meaning of revolution, clarifying revolutionary theories, and encouraging revolutionary courage, so that the national masses were awakened from their dreams and participated in the revolutionary movement to overthrow the Qing government. Therefore, Mr. Zhu and Mr. Hu Hanmin, Mr. Dai Jitao, and Mr. Liao Zhongkai were the four strongmen who helped the Prime Minister promote the revolution through writing in the beginning. Mr. Zhu not only worked hard to promote the revolution through writing, but also worked very hard in action. Mr. Zhu presided over everything in the Battle of Zhennanguan. Mr. Zhu also participated in the Battle of Huanghuagang on March 29th. Initially, Mr. Zhu was wearing a bamboo cloth long gown. He felt that the long gown was inconvenient, so he cut it in half and led many comrades to rush into the Guangzhou yamen. Although he did not suffer misfortune that time, he was seriously injured. Later, Mr. Zhu also participated in the battles to punish Yuan and protect the law. If the counter-revolutionaries were not eliminated for one day, Mr. Zhu's fighting spirit and revolutionary courage would not stop for one day. Therefore, Mr. Zhu never stopped fighting in his life and fought to the death with the reactionaries. Finally, he was murdered by the Gui系 warlords. Mr. Zhu finally sacrificed for the revolution in the ninth year of the Republic of China. This is a general overview of Mr. Zhu's revolutionary work in his life. At the same time, Mr. Zhu also had several virtues that ordinary people could not possess. The first is the spirit of thrift and simplicity. Mr. Zhu wore cloth clothes and trousers, ate green vegetables and light meals, and the house he lived in was especially narrow and simple. When he was in exile in Japan in the beginning, his economy was very difficult, but when comrades from other provinces asked him to borrow money, he never refused. Even if he did not have it himself, he tried to find a way to help others. The second is Mr. Zhu's active fighting spirit. Mr. Zhu encountered many difficulties and hardships in his life, but he was not at all passive. He always said generously to the revolutionary party members who retreated in the face of difficulties and deserted in the face of battle: "We eat the food of the common people, wear the clothes of the common people, and live in the houses of the common people. If we don't do things for the common people, can we still be considered human beings?" How could he not know that the reactionaries wanted to get him, but he was not afraid, not afraid, and not passive at all. He would rather be sniped by the reactionaries than be afraid of the reactionaries' plot to survive and stop the revolutionary work. He had a revolutionary outlook on life of living for the revolution and dying for the revolution, so he cultivated an active fighting spirit. Third, Mr. Zhu's profound knowledge was beyond the reach of ordinary comrades. Mr. Dai Jitao said that Mr. Zhu read more books than I did and had a higher understanding, so his knowledge was also higher than mine. Mr. Sun Yat-sen said that Chen Yingshi's understanding of the revolution was very accurate, and his revolutionary spirit was also beyond the reach of ordinary people, but his knowledge was a little lacking. Zhixin's understanding and spirit of the revolution were about the same as Yingshi's, but Zhixin's knowledge was much higher than Yingshi's. Mr. Hu Hanmin also said that Mr. Zhu Zhixin was able to integrate the theories of famous scholars in the world. Of course, it was Mr. Zhixin's hard work, but it was also Mr. Zhixin's great and unique point. Now it has been ten years since Mr. Zhu was murdered by the reactionaries. Today, ten years later, the reverse flame of the reactionaries has not been completely eliminated, and the imperialists' oppression of China is becoming more and more serious every day. The responsibility after the sacrifice of the martyrs is to be borne by us who died later. Today, we commemorate Mr. Zhu's martyrdom, understand Mr. Zhu's revolutionary life, and understand Mr. Zhu's spirit of struggle and learning. We should learn from Mr. Zhu and continue Mr. Zhu's spirit, personality, and career to complete China's difficult and hard revolutionary work. Now the political situation in the north has fallen into total collapse, and the elimination of the rebels Yan Feng and Wang is no longer a problem. However, how to build a new Republic of China after the reactionary forces are eliminated, how to realize the Prime Minister's will, and how to relieve the suffering of the Chinese people in the era of suffering. I hope that all comrades and representatives from all walks of life present at today's memorial service for Mr. Zhu Zhixin's martyrdom should deeply reflect and make real efforts. The report is over.

Representative Speeches

Tao Baichuan said in his speech, "Fellow comrades, today is the tenth anniversary of Mr. Zhu Zhixin's martyrdom. We are holding a meeting today to commemorate him. I believe that not only are we in Shanghai holding a meeting to commemorate him, but also all places in the country where the Kuomintang's power reaches are holding meetings to commemorate him. Not only are we commemorating him now, but also in the past, since Mr. Zhu Zhixin's martyrdom, everyone who knows Mr. Zhu has been commemorating him. Not only is this true in the past and present, but I believe that in the future, twenty weeks later, I believe that commemorating Mr. Zhu and mourning Mr. Zhu will definitely be more and more enthusiastic. There have been many people who sacrificed for the country in the past, but why do we commemorate Mr. Nian so enthusiastically? The reasons for this have been reported in detail by the chairman in the past, and the spirit, career, and personality of Mr. Zhu have been introduced in detail and succinctly. I would like to raise a point to explain in detail. I think the reason why Mr. Zhu is worthy of our commemoration is the word 'public' in the world. Mr. Zhu's lifelong career was for the public, and Mr. Zhu's death was also for the public. Death is not a strange thing. We will never commemorate him because Mr. Zhu died so tragically. At the same time, Mr. Zhu was always prepared to die when he wrote articles and spoke in his life, because a revolutionary party member had already determined the fate of death when he stepped on the revolutionary front. Death is not strange. Of course, we don't have to commemorate Mr. Zhu because he died so tragically. We commemorate Mr. Zhu because Mr. Zhu did not die for personal gain, for fame and fortune, or for sensual pleasures. He died entirely for the public, so he deserves our admiration. The ninth year of the Republic of China happened to be the end of the European War. In the four years from the fourth year of the Republic of China to the eighth year of the Republic of China, international imperialists, except for Japan, were busy fighting among themselves and had no time to take care of China. However, by the ninth year of the Republic of China, the European War had ended, and the imperialists, when they were exhausted and economically exhausted, tried their best to invade China and wanted to compensate for all their losses during the European War in China. Therefore, their invasion and oppression were ten or a hundred times more fierce than before. Mr. Sun Yat-sen witnessed this dangerous situation and knew that to resist the powers and resist the oppression of the imperialists, there must be a strong and unified government. However, at that time, the Northern Warlords were arrogant and wanted to resist the powers by calling on the warlords, which was tantamount to seeking skin from a tiger and was absolutely impossible. The South was relatively hopeful, so Mr. Sun Yat-sen decided to make Guangdong a revolutionary base and sent Mr. Zhu to Guangzhou to contact the people's groups and organize the masses, wanting to drive out the warlords of the Gui系 in Guangzhou. Therefore, Mr. Zhu died at the hands of the warlords. Therefore, Mr. Zhu's death was to save the country from collapse, to save the nation from danger, and to relieve the suffering of the people. In short, Mr. Zhu died for the public. Therefore, Mr. Zhu's death is very different from the death of ordinary people. Now the Kuomintang's power has spread throughout the country, and the number of Kuomintang members has also increased compared to before. However, how many people can live and die for the public like Mr. Zhu? Take Shanghai as an example. How many comrades in Shanghai can strive for the public and sacrifice for the public like Mr. Zhu? Shanghai is the place where the oppression and invasion of imperialism are most obvious. However, we ask ourselves whether every civilian in Shanghai understands, is used to, and is ready to struggle and sacrifice with the imperialists. Even if they understand the oppression of the imperialists and are determined to fight to the death with the imperialists, how many can there be? Let's take the boycott of foreign goods as an example. How many civilians can firmly and eternally extend their determination to boycott? The weakness of this national consciousness and the collapse of the national spirit is because everyone only knows about private matters and doesn't know about public matters. When it comes to national affairs, many people criticize the authorities for being wrong and making mistakes. If you ask him to help the government and do something, he will decline politely and slip away. Shunmin saves the country, it's not my business, there are Zhou Gong and Confucius. These two lines of poetry describe the attitude of our people towards national affairs, which can be said to be very accurate. This shows that the people of our country only know how to curse and sing high-pitched tunes, but they will not actually work hard to do it. The reason for this is that everyone only knows about private matters and doesn't know about public matters. The domestic disasters are so serious, and the suffering of the victims crying for food is not something we can describe. However, rich people would rather eat and drink, watch movies, go to gambling casinos, visit dance halls, and do all kinds of other sensual things. If you want him to donate money to help the victims, he is willing to pull out a hair to benefit the world. This is a manifestation of only knowing about private matters and not knowing about public matters. How many people die in Shanghai every day? Many rich and wealthy people are killed by bandits. Many bandits die for bandit cases. Many people commit suicide because they fail to steal women, as well as many other people who die for sensual pleasures and fame and fortune. Not only do we not give them the slightest sympathy or regret for the deaths of these people, but we also denounce and curse them. The reason for this is that they died for private gain and not for the public. Therefore, today we commemorate Mr. Zhu's martyrdom. First, we should learn from Mr. Zhu's spirit of dying for the public. Now it is the nineteenth year of the Republic of China, and it has been exactly ten years since Mr. Zhu's martyrdom in the ninth year of the Republic of China. Is the situation better than before? The oppression of imperialism is more and more serious, and the harassment of the reactionaries is still constant. The foundation of the National Government is still very fragile, and the foundation of the Republic of China is still very shaky. China in the era of suffering is still in need of people like Mr. Zhu who are for the country and the people, who live for the public and die for the public. We really feel very sad and empty. How many people in our party are like Mr. Zhu who are for the public? In addition to being afraid and trembling, how should we learn from Mr. Zhu's spirit, personality, and career to complete Mr. Zhu's unfinished business? If everyone still only knows about private matters, lives for private gain, and dies for private gain, then the country and the nation will certainly have no way to do it, and those who seek welfare for private gain will also be limited to the fate of destruction, because China needs people like Mr. Zhu who are dedicated to the public. Therefore, I will contribute this point to you. The speech is over.

Lawyers Association Held a General Meeting Yesterday

The Shanghai Lawyers Association convened a general meeting in the autumn yesterday (Sunday). From 1:00 pm to 3:00 pm, 102 members arrived successively. The Shanghai Local Court and the Special District Local Court both sent prosecutors to supervise the meeting. The association has a total of 541 members. After deducting 96 members who owe fees, the statutory number of members must be 112. At 3:30 pm, a discussion meeting was held first. The members of the presidium, Liu Zuwang, Tan Yigong, and Jiang Yiping (replaced by Chen Tingrui), took their seats, and Dai Jixian recorded the meeting. The details of the meeting are recorded below: 1. Ring the bell to open the meeting. 2. All stand at attention and bow three times to the party's national flag. 3. Chairman Liu Zuwang respectfully reads the Prime Minister's will. 4. Reporting matters: (A) General affairs, (B) Documents, (C) Accounting. After the reports were completed, more than ten members arrived, which was enough to meet the statutory number of members. The general meeting was then opened, and the proposals were submitted for discussion. (A) The National Lawyers Association sent a letter to the association requesting an additional one-tenth donation (the original proposal was to collect the donation together with the regular fees paid by the members). Zhang Feixiong, Li Shirui, Yang Chunlv, Shan Yuhua, Wu Mai, and others expressed their opinions and discussed the results. It was resolved that the association would donate 600 yuan annually from July of the 19th year to the end of June of the 20th year, and the case was handed over to the executive and supervisory committees for handling. (B) Should the representatives attending the National Lawyers Association be re-elected? Member Li Shirui stood up and reported that the Lawyers Association was scheduled to hold a general meeting in Hangzhou in April of next year to re-elect the representatives. It was too early to re-elect the representatives. The re-election should be discussed at the spring meeting next year. The resolution was passed. (C) Qu Yue, Wang Chenggu, Liang Dihua, Chen Tingrui, and other sixteen people proposed that there was no need to divide the lawyer's rest room in the Shanghai Special District Local Court under the current situation.

Page 14

It was resolved to hand it over to the executive and supervisory committees for handling. (D) Member Shen Xiaoxiang proposed that the association should establish a library. Chairman Tan Yigong reported that it was originally intended to build a grand auditorium first and attach the library to it. After the original proposer reported the reasons for the proposal, it was resolved to take two steps: first, establish a preparatory library; second, discuss the construction of the grand auditorium and decide to hand over the matter to the executive and supervisory committees for active handling. (E) Member Wang Fuguo proposed that a request be submitted to the Ministry of Justice to establish county courts in various counties of Jiangsu on schedule. It was resolved to submit it to the next executive and supervisory committee for discussion and handling. After discussion by the public, it was resolved that the matter was important and should be left to the joint meeting of the executive and supervisory committees for discussion. At 6:30 pm, refreshments were served and the meeting adjourned.

Committee for Revising the Articles of Association of the Red Cross

Continues to Meet

The Committee for Revising the Articles of Association of the Chinese Red Cross Society held its 15th meeting at 2:00 PM on September 19th. The committee members present were Li Zhenbang, Wen Lanting, Wang Peiyuan, Dong Xinqin, Yang Ke, Jiang Daqiu, Xu Xichun, Wu Jiasan, Ye Zhisheng, Wang Xiaolai, Liu Hongsheng, Xue Shaoting, and Hong Yanbin. Wen Lanting served as chairman and Wei Ruifeng recorded the minutes. The usual formalities were observed. The minutes of the previous meeting were read, and without objection, the chairman signed them.

The chairman made a temporary motion that the rules of procedure for the meeting be temporarily retained, and that the regulations of the executive committee and the simplified rules for the sub-offices of the executive committee be read for the third time today.

Jiang Daqiu proposed that the regulations of the executive committee and the simplified rules for the sub-offices could be combined into one, and the name changed to "Detailed Rules of the Executive Committee of the Red Cross Society of the Republic of China."

Wu Jiasan suggested that in Article 1, the words "this committee" could be followed by parentheses adding "hereinafter referred to as 'the Association'."

Jiang Daqiu proposed that Article 2 should be changed to "The powers of the Association shall be exercised in accordance with the provisions of the general regulations and decided by meetings." Also, Article 3 should be changed to "The Association shall conduct its affairs, and in the event of temporary emergency matters that cannot be submitted to the Standing Committee for approval, they must be submitted to the Standing Committee for ratification after implementation." Furthermore, Article 4 could be deleted.

Dong Xinqin proposed that Article 5, "Publicly elect one person as chairman" should be changed to "Not elect one person as temporary chairman."

Jiang Daqiu proposed that Article 6, "If the chairman and vice-chairman cannot be permanently located at the Association's location, one of the vice-chairmen should be designated as the permanent representative in Shanghai to be responsible, etc.," should be changed to "If the chairman and vice-chairman cannot be located at the headquarters, they should mutually designate one person as the permanent representative in Shanghai to be responsible." Also, Article 8, "The Association shall meet once a week" should be changed to "The Association shall meet weekly." Articles 9 and 10 should be interchanged, and Article 9 should be changed to "If a member is absent due to important matters, they must authorize another member to represent them in writing."

Dong Xinqin proposed that Article 10 should be changed to "When matters that the Standing Committee has decided should be implemented, and difficulties arise in implementation, the Association may submit reasons to the Standing Committee requesting reconsideration." Also, Article 11, "However, the representatives sent by one branch shall not exceed two persons" can be deleted.

Jiang Daqiu proposed that Article 12 could be deleted, and Article 13, "Handle all matters of the Association" could also be deleted. "Separate rules for the sub-offices and operating procedures shall be formulated" should be changed to "Operating procedures shall be formulated separately," and Articles 3, 4, 5, 6, 7, and 8 of the simplified rules for the sub-offices should be moved below Article 13.

Dong Xinqin proposed that the original Article 3, "The duties of the document section are as follows, all items..." should be changed to: "1. Drafting and translation of correspondence and telegrams; 2. Compilation and storage of files and archives; 3. Custody of official seals and chops; 4. Writing and sending of correspondence and all documents; 5. Custody and issuance of certificates and articles of association; 6. Registration of members and compilation of the roll of honor."

The original item 6 under Article 3, "Duties of the Relief Department are as follows..." could be deleted.

Jiang Daqiu proposed that Article 5, "Duties of the Medical Department are as follows..." should be changed: "1. Supervise the affairs of hospitals affiliated with the headquarters; 2. Plan the promotion and expansion of hospitals affiliated with the headquarters." Yang Ke suggested that: "3. Plan hospitals to be established by various branches."

Jiang Daqiu proposed that Article 6 should be changed to: "Promote epidemic prevention and sanitation campaigns on various matters," and "Establish schools for volunteer doctors and nurses."

Also, Article 7, "Duties of the Youth Department are as follows..." should be changed to: "1. Recruit youth members; 2. Promote youth members; 4. Guide various branches in handling youth affairs; 7. Promote the development of youth education; 8. Manage the communication of youth members of Red Cross societies in various countries."

The chairman proposed that item 5 of the original Article 8 could be deleted and a new item "Compilation of a credit rating record" added as item 6.

Jiang Daqiu proposed that after Article 8 of the Simplified Rules for Sub-Offices, the original Article 14 in the Regulations should be added. The original Article 15 should be changed to "Directors must attend Executive Committee meetings to report on handled matters," and the original Article 10 in the Simplified Rules for Sub-Offices should be changed to "Each department may establish one director and several clerks and secretaries depending on the workload, nominated by the department heads and approved by the Executive Committee, to be appointed and dismissed by the chairman, but concurrent positions may not receive concurrent pay." Also, the original Article 16 in the Regulations should be changed to "A person designated by the document section shall be the recorder at meetings of the Association and organize the motions," and the original Articles 17 and 18 should be listed consecutively afterward. The original Article 18, after being revised by Jiang Daqiu, should be changed to: "Members of the Association may propose those with a deep and lengthy history with the Association and who are enthusiastic philanthropists, or those with experience in the medical field, to be consultants of the Association, subject to the approval of the Standing Committee and appointment by the Chairman as honorary positions, and may be invited to attend meetings of the Association to provide advice." Also, the original Article 19 should be changed to: "Supplementary Provisions."

The chairman reported that the detailed rules of the Executive Committee have been read for the third time. The meeting will continue tomorrow to organize the various articles of association passed on the third reading. The meeting adjourned at five o'clock.

Reduced Train Fares for Cooperative Society Members

The traffic departments of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways yesterday issued a notice to station masters and ticket sellers at all stations, stating: "Recently, we received an order from the Railway Administration, which in turn received an order from the Ministry of Railways approving a letter from the Chinese Cooperative Society stating that the society will hold a meeting in Hangzhou from October 3rd to 19th, and requesting that all participating members be given half-price fares as a convenience." Enclosed are 50 copies each of the member list and sample travel passes. The Ministry has granted a convenience and approved a 25% discount for one-way tickets and a 50% discount for round-trip tickets. However, this must be handled in accordance with the fare reduction restrictions of each railway. In addition to issuing separate orders, we are also sending 25 copies each of the original list and sample travel passes. You are to comply with this order and instruct the stations to verify the society's certificates and exchange them for train tickets, collecting fares accordingly."

Upon investigation, there are approximately 120 members of the society who will be traveling from Beijing, Nanjing, Zhenjiang, Jiangsu, Shanghai North Station, Shanghai South Station, and Songjiang to attend the meeting in Hangzhou within the specified period. Each member will exchange their certificate at the respective station for a round-trip ticket at half the ordinary fare. The minimum first-class fare is $1.00 per person, second-class is $0.75, and third-class is $0.50. However, these fares do not apply to express trains on the two lines. If passengers need to take the Beijing-Shanghai Railway's night express trains 27 and 28, or the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway's train 49, additional fares must be charged. You are to comply accordingly.

Scope of Application of the Land Expropriation Law

The Municipal Government Issues Orders to Respective Departments to Comply

The Shanghai Municipal Government recently received an instruction from the Executive Yuan, stating roughly: "Based on a case presented by the Civil Affairs Department of this government, approved by the Secretariat of the Central Executive Committee, concerning the Nanjing Special Municipality Executive Committee forwarding a petition from the First Branch of the Tenth District requesting the government to issue a general order to all agencies that when expanding office buildings and constructing staff dormitories, they may not invoke the Land Expropriation Law to expropriate land from the people. The current explanation of the Land Expropriation Law allows for the expropriation of land for the construction of office buildings by various customs offices. However, it does not seem applicable to the construction of staff dormitories. It is forwarded for review and implementation." It was approved that "The use of the Land Expropriation Law to expropriate land from the people for the use of customs office staff dormitories is indeed inappropriate. A general order should be sent to the National Government instructing all agencies that they may not use the construction of dormitories as a pretext to expropriate land from the people." In addition to replying, we have copied the original petition and forwarded it for your information and hope you will forward it for handling. We approve this proposal and instruct you to handle it accordingly. In addition to replying, we are also issuing orders to the departments and agencies within the city to comply.

Yesterday

Overseas Chinese from Malaya Return to China, Arriving in Shanghai

Five from Hunan and Hubei

The Taikoo Company's Xinjiang steamship arrived from Hong Kong yesterday, carrying five elderly and frail overseas Chinese from the Malay Peninsula, originally from Hunan and Hubei provinces. They described the reasons for returning to their homeland, stating that since the price of tin fell in the Malay Peninsula, unemployment among overseas Chinese has been increasing. While the strong can support themselves, the elderly and frail have nowhere to find food. This group consists of more than 160 people, mostly from Guangdong and Fujian, who were assisted by the consulate in Penang and the Ping Foon Association for repatriation by the Chinese Civil Affairs Department. After a medical examination, they were deemed incapable of labor and boarded the "Mountain Chu" ship in early September, arriving in Hong Kong and then transferring to the "Xinjiang" ship to Shanghai. They will return to their native provinces today. "We have been away from our hometowns for more than thirty years, and we are very pleased to see the scenery of our motherland today. The rapid progress of various industries in the motherland makes it seem like another world."

The National Walking Corps

The Reason for Temporarily Suspending Progress

The National Walking Corps has been on its way for nearly half a year since its departure, and after several setbacks, it finally arrived in Xianghe County, Hebei Province, a month ago. Due to the impact of the current situation, it could not move forward and had to temporarily suspend its progress to await an opportunity to continue. Now, the members of the Corps have returned to Shanghai in order, and during this period of suspension, they will organize the records of the journey over the past six months for publication, and their photos will also be developed and put on public display. Yesterday, the Corps issued a special circular detailing the process and the reasons for the temporary suspension. We have selected the key points to record below: "We spent more than six months, through the howling wind and scorching sun, walking to Peiping after many twists and turns. Unfortunately, we encountered unexpected obstacles in Peiping. However, our courage will not be diminished in the slightest. We still moved forward regardless, but unfortunately we could not pass through Xianghe (Hebei) and were forced to temporarily suspend our work. We set out from Shanghai to Nanjing, and went up the Huai River to the East China Sea. Our original plan was to travel through Suqian and Muyang to Xuzhou. When we came down from Yuntai Mountain, war clouds were already looming over the Jinpu Railway Line and bandits were rampant in eastern Shandong, so we had to change our plan. We reluctantly took a boat from Xinpu to Qingdao, planning to go to Jinan via the Jiaoji Railway and then along the Jinpu Railway to Tianjin. We heard that the northern section of the Jinpu Railway was still calm, but on the fourth day after we arrived in Qingdao, the Central Army abandoned Jinan and the situation changed suddenly, becoming more tense than before. Therefore, the motive to take the Jinpu Railway had to be abandoned, so we decided to abandon Shandong, leaving it to be visited later. We took a boat from Qingdao to Tianjin, preparing to go out through the Beining Railway. When we contacted the Beining Railway Bureau to ask them to transport our luggage, a section chief advised us, saying that the current situation is not good, and that people will suspect you Southerners for coming here, and the garrison may misunderstand and not understand, which could cause unexpected dangers. Moreover, you cannot do any survey work at this time, which would be futile. Furthermore, there are many bandits along the line, and the trains still need armed guards. You should consider it carefully. We were very grateful for the section chief's sincere guidance, so we decided to go to Peiping first during this military period and ask the provincial government to issue a certificate of proof, which might be more convenient than explaining to the local military and police with empty words. Who knew that as soon as we arrived in Peiping, we lost our freedom of action. The military and police authorities could not understand our undertaking. They did not know what we seven or eight unfamiliar Southerners were doing. No matter how much you talked, they would not understand. Later, we finally got released through a series of connections, but they were always uneasy. After staying in Peiping for a long time, the war was still fierce and the Beining Railway was washed away by floods. We received a tour passport and immediately prepared to pass through Tongzhou, Sanhe, Yutian, etc. and exit Shanhaiguan regardless of everything. Unexpectedly, we were stopped as soon as we arrived in Tongzhou, so we turned to Xianghe, but we could not pass through either. The hotels in the county town dared not accommodate us, and the military and police secretly monitored our actions. We could not get freedom of action, let alone go to the countryside to conduct on-the-spot investigations. At this time, we could have gone directly to the three northeastern provinces or changed our route to the south, but during this unstable period, our work would inevitably make people suspicious. Even if the authorities could understand, the public would be frightened and would suspect that we had some purpose and would not be willing to talk to us. Therefore, we finally temporarily suspended our progress. This is the phenomenon we have experienced since our departure. When we recall the expectations of the people in Shanghai and the support and sympathy expressed by people in various places along the way, we are very ashamed. However, this group of ours will never collapse. Our courage is still as strong as before, and we will never be discouraged. We recognize that the past is an attempt, a failure that has increased a lot of our experience. As soon as the overall situation stabilizes, we will continue our second effort. If the second time is unsuccessful, we will try three or four times until we finally complete our original plan to live up to the expectations of society. During this period of suspension, we can complete the following two tasks: 1. Organize the materials collected from various places and attach them to the departure commemorative album; 2. Develop the photos, attach detailed explanations, and display them together with the specimens in public, and hope that people from all walks of life and enthusiastic comrades will participate. The mailing address is still No. 608, Rue P. Froc."

Wusong Anti-Smuggling Captain on Patrol

Recently, due to the unrest among pirates in the outer seas, Li Huchen, captain of the first anti-smuggling detachment of Wusong, led team captain Gao Song and the team on ten patrol boats from Wusong at about 7:00 AM yesterday. They first patrolled the islands of Hengsha and Yawo Sha, and then went up the river to patrol Liuhe, Fushan, Hupu, Baimao and other places, and inspected the defenses of the teams stationed in various locations. It will take about a week to return to Wusong for defense.

Shaanxi Province Appeals for Aid Due to Recent Disasters

Jisheng Society Reports Successive Testimonies

The Chinese Jisheng Society has repeatedly received letters from Liu, Chairman of the Shaanxi Provincial Government via the Chang'an Branch of Shaanxi Province. The letter states that "In Shaanxi, the disasters of soldiers, bandits, famine and devastation have multiplied, and the deaths are overwhelming. The disaster situation is unprecedented since ancient times. Fortunately, the gentlemen of your society have a compassionate heart and can generously help the people. The kindness of life and death permeates the surviving. This is not only the gratitude of millions of Taian people who are waiting to die, but also the joint praise of me and my colleagues, and we will never forget your great virtue. However, it is difficult to reverse the will of Heaven, and the calamity has not ended. In addition, locusts are causing havoc, and the disaster has lasted for three years. If it were not for your society's multi-faceted rescue, could we hope that there would still be survivors? We hope that you will continue to provide assistance to complete the work." We have also received telegrams from the Shaanxi disaster victims' representatives, stating that "The great disaster has not ended, and locusts, wolves and rats continue to cause havoc. More than 4 million disaster victims have died in ditches due to plague and hunger. Fortunately, your society's rescue has slightly reduced the deaths, but the autumn is dry and locusts are followed by wind and hail. There is no hope for a harvest, and the survivors are waiting to die. We ask you to publicize the appeal and quickly raise relief funds to reduce the catastrophe to a minimum." After investigating the situation of the disaster in Shaanxi, which has been recorded in previous reports, the situation has become even worse recently, according to reports. The society is currently setting up disaster victim and disaster child shelters in Shaanxi Province to provide emergency relief. However, the disaster is great and the funds are small, so how can this help? We can only appeal to compatriots to join hands for assistance. Life and death are at stake, and we hope for the ultimate blessing. Millions of disaster victims are enduring death and leading the way to wait.

Game Hall Tickets Must Have Stamps Affixed

Wang and Guan, directors of the Jiangsu Province Stamp Tax Bureau and the Customs Bureau, are very serious about handling stamp duties in the concessions. Merchants in the concessions who have failed to affix stamps have been investigated and fined in the Special District Local Court because the Municipal Council has agreed to provide assistance. More than twenty households were fined last Saturday. Now, Wang and Guan believe that the tickets sold at theaters and game halls in the Public Concession must also have stamps affixed. Tickets with a value of more than one corner must have a one-cent stamp affixed. Since the tickets for the "Fairy World" are worth only one corner, they are exempt from stamps. Therefore, "Hua Hua World" has also reduced the price of its tickets to one corner recently. Other game halls have not been able to reduce their prices due to high expenses and would rather comply with the regulations and purchase stamps. However, the Beijing Opera theaters are still in consultation. It is said that the Beijing Opera theaters are willing to wholesale a certain number of stamps every day, while the tax bureau insists on purchasing stamps for each ticket. Each party has its own reasons, so negotiations are still underway.

Minutes of the Meeting of the Five-Neighborhood Joint Association of Tenants

Since the landlord of the tenants in the five neighborhoods of Ximen Road in the French Concession announced a rent increase, the tenants, considering the economic depression and the hardship of the people's livelihood, found it difficult to bear the sudden increase in rent. Therefore, they organized a tenants' association to negotiate with the landlord to cancel the rent increase. The tenants convened a second meeting at the original location at 7:00 PM the day before yesterday. Fifty-six people attended. Chairman Liu Yunsheng reported on the landlord's lawyer's reply. After the tenants expressed their opinions, they decided on the following countermeasures: 1. Refute the landlord's lawyer's reply with reason; 2. All tenants unite to reject the rent increase; 3. Petition the Municipal Party Headquarters, the French Concession Chinese Taxpayers' Association, the Tenants' General Federation and other organizations to uphold justice and provide assistance; 4. Pay all October rent at the original amount. If the landlord does not accept it, deposit it in the bank to avoid the landlord using it as an excuse; 5. The association will produce slogans and distribute them to the members to post to show the spirit of unity and promote the landlord's awareness; 6. All expenses will be borne by all; 7. Hire a lawyer as the legal advisor of the association. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Address Change for the Party Headquarters of the Two Railways

The Party Headquarters of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways, which has been located at No. 257 Bazilu, has been repeatedly requested to relocate because the Railway Bureau is going to convert the building into a hospital, and has separately designated No. 1392 North Sichuan Road (next to the Tiantong'an Station) as the new office address. Therefore, the Party Headquarters moved on the 20th. It is rumored that the building is very spacious and the air is quite clean, but the portion allocated is too small and there is still a lack of auditorium, so it needs to be contacted with the Railway Bureau again.

The Anglo-American Tobacco Factory Union held its fifth executive committee election conference yesterday at the Pudong Grand Theater. 175 representatives attended, with guests including Chen Jinliang, representative of the No. 2 Defense Corps; Cheng Pengyun, representative of the Third District Public Security Bureau; Shu Ronghan, representative of the Fourth Platoon of the Police; Tao Ze, representative of the Third Battalion Headquarters; Xia Menghuan, representative of the Fifth District Party Headquarters; Zhou Funong and Wu Jiaze, representatives of the Municipal Party Headquarters' Civil Training Committee, as well as representatives from various labor unions and organizations, totaling several dozen people. After the presidium's report, the heads of each department reported on the fourth session's work summary. Then, the following proposals were passed: 1. In addition, the following suggestions were proposed: 1. The union's standing committee members must take turns to stay overnight daily. 2. Please establish a worker's clinic and hire Dr. Wang Depei to provide regular consultations. 3. The union's membership fees must be collected by union representatives entering the factory. 4. Please appoint the union's children's school's directors to be stationed at the school regularly to supervise school affairs. 6. Please develop the union's work implementation outline and operating rules. 7. Please request the factory to build a workshop. 8. Please organize a consumer cooperative. 9. Please increase the union's service wages. 10. Please organize the Anglo-American Tobacco Factory Third Factory Union. The above eight proposals were resolved to be handled and discussed by the new fifth executive committee. After the discussion was completed, the election began. As a result, Chen Peide, Gu Ruofeng, Xiao Gengsheng, Liu Dehua, Fei Keguang, Pan Shanrong, Xia Su'e, Li Guangxian, Chen Shaoqing, Dong Aosheng, Ye Huibing, Xie Peiji, Zhang Ziping, Ren Kun Da, Wang A'jin, Hu Xiaomei, Bao Yangzhou, Zhang Peisheng, Chen Haiqing, Sun Qingyou, Shen Baokang, Sun Ronggui, Ying Qipei, Zhang Yuqing, and Zhu Ahao, twenty-five people, were elected as executive committee members.
