Local News Two

Famous Doctor of Hongkou

Zhu Ziyun is Kidnapped

Kidnappers Drag Zhu Out of the Door

In Haste, He Couldn't Even Put on His Shoes

Waiting Patients Were All Amazed

Zhu Suffers from Diabetes and Hasn't Eaten for a Long Time

The Throat Specialist's Practice is Always Crowded

Dr. Zhu Ziyun, a throat specialist famous in Hongkou, suddenly had his residence tightly closed yesterday afternoon. No one was there, and a note was posted on the door saying, "Temporarily closed for business." Zhu's accountant, Qi Gai, posted the note. This famous doctor of Hongkou, Zhu Ziyun, was suddenly kidnapped by bandits from his consulting room at around 11:00 AM yesterday. In such a hurry, not only did his brother, who was sitting across from him, not have time to say goodbye, but he didn't even have time to put on his shoes. Such an embarrassing situation was truly unexpected. The house has three layers of doors. The famous doctor Zhu Ziyun is the son of Zhu Baoqing, a throat specialist from a long line of doctors. He and his brother Zhongyun run a clinic together at 3151 Zhoujiazui Road. Even women and children in the Hongkou area know of his reputation. It is said that he sees around 150 patients every day. At most, he sees 180, 190, or even 200 patients. There are very few famous doctors in Shanghai who can compare to him. Zhu's consulting room is located in the main hall. Entering through the main gate, you first pass through the wall gate, then the courtyard, and then the main hall. Every day, hundreds of patients are here. They receive Zhu Ziyun's pulse-taking, tongue examination, prescription, and medication. The house faces south, and Zhu sits facing north, with patients on his left and a doorman on his right. He takes pulses and prescribes medication. Anyone who enters must first see Mr. Zhu's back, nod, and bow among the patients.

Brothers Sitting Across from Each Other

Because Zhu has too many patients every day and is mentally exhausted, his brother Zhongyun assists with the clinic's affairs. His seat is set up across from Zhu. The brothers sit together at one table. Yesterday morning, Zhu Ziyun was already in the consulting room seeing patients at around 8:00 AM. By about 11:00 AM, there were still 30 to 40 people waiting to be seen, so there were many people entering and exiting. At that time, three men suddenly entered through the main gate and went straight into the main hall, without registering or asking any questions.

Dragging Zhu Out

These three men walked up behind Zhu. One of them said, "I'm sorry for today." Before Zhu could turn around, two of them grabbed him and pointed three guns at him. Zhu didn't even have time to put on his shoes before being dragged out of his seat straight towards the main gate. Zhu's brother Zhongyun was greatly shocked to see his brother suddenly leave his seat, and the patients in the room were also surprised. It wasn't until Zhu got into the car that everyone realized that these were kidnappers who had come to kidnap him. The news of Zhu Ziyun's kidnapping instantly spread throughout the streets. Since Zhu had suffered misfortune, his brother Zhongyun also temporarily closed the clinic. All the patients had no choice but to withdraw their tickets and get their consultation fees back.

Travelers Rent a Car

An hour before Zhu Ziyun was kidnapped, Chen Xiaonan, a traveler from Zhenhua Hotel at 68 Guangxi Road, rented car number 17625 from Haoyou Automobile Company. This car was used to kidnap Zhu. Previously, a traveler claiming to be Chen Xiaonan from Ningbo arrived at Zhenhua Hotel on Fuzhou Road at around 5:00 PM on the 19th and rented room number 68. At around 10:00 AM yesterday, he ordered the room service to rent a car from Haoyou Automobile Company to take him to Bazilu. The room service walked to Haoyou Automobile Company to rent the car. The accountant ordered the driver Lu Asi to drive the Chevrolet car number 17625 (Municipal 4574) to the customer.

Jiangwan Watching the Land

Lu drove the car to the entrance of Zhenhua Hotel, and a man in his thirties wearing a khaki robe opened the door and got in. Just as he was about to drive off, another person came forward, greeted the person in the car briefly, and also got in. They instructed the driver to drive to Bazilu, turn onto Jiangwan Road, and stop near Zhizhi University. Two other people were already waiting by the side of the road. They walked into the fields to look at the land. Who knew that in a turn, the driver Lu Asi was suddenly dragged out of the driver's seat by two people and dragged into the graveyard. His mouth was stuffed with cotton to prevent him from making any noise, while the other two people stole the car. About an hour later, the driver managed to escape and ran back to Shanghai to report. By this time, Zhu Ziyun had already been kidnapped. Car number 1762 was found in the afternoon.

Kidnapping Zhu Ziyun

After stealing this car, the bandits drove it to Zhoujiazui Road to kidnap Zhu Ziyun. After getting the "God of Wealth," the car drove west towards Sikaizi Bridge and disappeared in an instant. Zhu developed diabetes last autumn and has been suffering from it for a long time. He has not recovered to this day. Following the advice of Western doctors, he has stopped eating rice. He only eats noodles and other foods instead. Therefore, after being kidnapped, he is afraid that the food in the bandit's den will not be adequate and will harm his health.

Two Gunshots

The Chauffeur is in Grave Danger

Both Bullets Hit the Car

Li Hanqing, a 47-year-old employee of Yitai Foreign Firm at 60 Jiangxi Road and a native of Suzhou, lives at 9 Caishou Lane, Julai Road, in the French Concession. Because Li's affairs are numerous, he purchased car number 1571 to replace walking and rented garage number 412 along the road. He hired a local driver, Xu Xinbao, 32 years old. Xu has only been working for Li since last autumn, not yet a year, and his pure and honest nature has earned him the owner's trust. Li usually has many social engagements and often returns late at night. At 12:15 yesterday morning, Li had just finished a banquet and returned home. The driver Xu Xinbao drove the car directly into the alley. The owner got out of the car and went inside. Xu then slowly reversed the car out of the alleyway, with the front of the car facing west, intending to drive the car into the parking garage. Just as he reached the entrance, two gunshots suddenly rang out from the east. One bullet hit the seat Xu was sitting on, and the other hit the left side of the car door. The aim seemed to be to hit Xu, but fortunately, it missed. After the thugs fired the shots, they assumed that Xu had been hit and fled. Seeing that they were far away, Xu quickly got out of the car and rushed to report to the owner. He examined his body and found no injuries. He immediately reported the situation to the police station. The detective immediately ordered the plainclothes detectives to investigate. After carefully inspecting the bullet holes in the car body, they reported back to the detective that there might be other circumstances involved. The police station is currently investigating. However, Li immediately fired Xu yesterday.

Old Man Missing in Zhangyan

Suffering from a Hidden Illness and Mental Disorder

Left the Hospital and Disappeared

Tang Shaoru, an old man from Zhangyan, Jinshan, is 77 years old. He is usually in good health and walks briskly. He has children and some assets and is considered well-off. Although he is old, he is still diligent and thrifty, and he still travels to Shanghai to engage in his cotton yarn business. At the beginning of August, he came to Shanghai from his hometown to negotiate business and temporarily stayed at a friend's place in the French Concession. Later, he suddenly developed a hidden illness in his lower body. On August 11, he was introduced by a friend to Dr. Shen Huimin, a female doctor at Ankang Lane, Yunnan Road, in the Public Concession, and was hospitalized for treatment. It has been more than a month. Although his illness is about to be cured, Tang, being so old, was unfortunately victimized by this disease. Suffering unexpectedly, he became depressed day and night, which led to mental disorder. On the afternoon of the 16th of this month, at about 7:30 PM, Tang suddenly left the hospital. At the time, it was suspected that he might have returned to his hometown as his illness was getting better. However, it was not until his family members came to Shanghai to visit him a few days ago that they learned that the old man had indeed disappeared. They immediately searched everywhere, but there was no trace of him. Yesterday, his family members reported to the Chinese and Public Concessions, requesting the police to pay attention to the matter. They are also offering a reward to find the old man. He was wearing a double blue twill short jacket, willow-striped cloth pants, white gauze socks, and black shoes. He is bald and has white hair. If anyone knows of his whereabouts, please contact Mr. Lu at 23 Shengping Lane, Dada Road.

Big Fire on Xiexu Road Yesterday Morning

Spreading to More Than Ten Households

Lasting for More Than Two Hours

At 8:10 AM yesterday, a fire suddenly broke out at the home of Zhang Xintang, a resident of No. 12, Alley 2, Deyun Lane, Xiexu Road, Nanshi. The fire brigades from various districts in Nanshi rushed to the scene after hearing the alarm. However, due to insufficient water pressure, the fire spread to ten households, lasting for two hours and fifty minutes. It was not until 11:05 AM that the fire was extinguished. The ten affected households were: No. 10 (Zhang A'ping, Tao Jiying, Sun A'yuan, Jin Shibiao), No. 11 (Cai Jinxiu, Wei A'xing, Shao Xiangzhou), No. 12 (Zhou Zhizeng), No. 13 (Lian Guangrong, Gao Lin, Song Rongfa, Hu Yuqing), No. 14 (Wan A'gen, Jin Shengcai, Jin Zijing), No. 29 (Chen Songlin, Zhou Anren, Shen Guo'shi, Han Heng),

The Dongjiadu Fire Brigade took photos while putting out the fire.

Shan Hu, Yun Shan, Chen Zhifan, No. 30 (Yu Rufa, Yuan Haiqing, Chen Yunqing, Zhang Jinxi, Wang Zifu, Chen Zuliang), No. 31 (Wang Jinshan, Chen A'mao, Xie Shaobo, Huang Weibiao), No. 32 (Wang Honggen), No. 33 (Zhou A'chen, Zhao Yingquan, Lu Guiquan), No. 34 (Sun Heshang, Zhao Keheng), etc., totaling 37 households. Gao Shiqiang, the inspector of the Second District Headquarters, arrived with several police officers to maintain order. Upon further investigation into the cause of the fire, the perpetrator had already fled in fear of punishment. Only Zhang's apprentice, Chen Tianfu, was detained at the headquarters. His statement was incoherent, and the cause of the fire was unclear. Furthermore, Chen's head was severely burned. The police were immediately ordered to send him to the hospital for treatment. The perpetrator, Zhang Xintang, is being strictly pursued for questioning.

Cholera Outbreaks Worsen After the Autumn Cool

Cholera was rare this summer, but dysentery was particularly prevalent, especially the bacterial type. Since the beginning of autumn, although dysentery has decreased, cholera has worsened. It is reported that the emergency epidemic hospital on North Xizang Road has been admitting many patients with cholera in recent days, and the number of saline injections given daily is invariably eight or nine people, totaling no less than several dozen people in the past few days. The ambulances are busy transporting patients back and forth.

Lawsuit After the Liquidation of Yuansheng Money Exchange

Partners Should Bear Unlimited Liability

Xia Juchuan Denies the Liquidation Terms

The Yuansheng Money Exchange, opened by Zhang Xingcun, a former compradore of Meifeng Bank, and others, has declared liquidation due to business losses. However, Xia Juchuan, a creditor of the exchange, believes that Yuansheng is a partnership and not a limited liability company, and should bear unlimited liability. He is unwilling to accept the liquidation terms. It is learned that the shareholders of the exchange were summoned by the Special District Local Court. The hearing continued the other day. The defendant Zhang Xingcun was represented by lawyers Zhang Deqin and Shen Yuesheng. However, because many of the defendants did not comply with the summons and did not appear in court, the hearing could not proceed. The judge instructed to summon the defendants to appear in court for further review.

Zhu Suzhen

Accuses Kong Jingqing of Failing to Provide Support

Kong Denies Taking Zhu as a Concubine

And Denies Having a Son

Kong Jingqing is fond of frequenting brothels. When he was working at the shop established by his father-in-law, he took the prostitute Zhu Suzhen as a concubine and hid her in a golden house on Dagu Road, without spending a penny on her dowry. After living together, he began to give her 200 yuan per month for household expenses. Zhu's decision to become a virtuous woman was due to her pregnancy after getting to know Kong. Before long, she gave birth to a son. However, Kong Suzhen was ungrateful and abandoned her after living together for a year. He stopped paying her household expenses and never visited Zhu's place again. Zhu had no choice but to take her child and rely on her mother for a living. Three years passed by, and the child grew up. Zhu realized that the days ahead were long, and she needed to solve the problems of her own livelihood and her son's education. Therefore, she demanded that Kong bear the responsibility of providing support. Kong denied taking Zhu as a concubine and denied that the child was his. Zhu then hired a lawyer to sue Kong in the Special District Local Court for abandonment and neglect, requesting a ruling to provide 20,000 yuan in alimony. After the initial hearing, the court ordered both parties to reconcile outside the court, but they were unable to reach a peaceful resolution. The case was heard again the other day. The defendant Kong Jingqing was unable to appear in court because he was suffering from severe lung disease and was being treated in the hospital. He sent a lawyer to represent him. The plaintiff Zhu Suzhen invited a female servant who was hired when she was a prostitute and a landlady surnamed, who was her landlord after she became Kong's concubine, to testify to everything that Kong had taken Zhu as a concubine that year. Judge Yang instructed to summon the defendant to appear in court for further questioning.

Cai Yunhai Case Scheduled for Sentencing

Cai Yunhai, the owner of the Cai Chen Import and Export Trading Company on Beijing Road, a native of Guangdong, was sued by a buyer because he failed to deliver the ordered foreign knives by the due date and did not return the deposit. The Special District Local Court summoned Cai and detained him in the civil detention center. However, Cai dared to escape by jumping out of the window late at night. Fearing that he would be wanted by the authorities, he surrendered himself to the prosecutor's office of the Special Court. Xu, the prosecutor, investigated the case together with the guards of the prison, Chen Jingcheng, etc. as previously reported. The investigation has now concluded, and it is believed that Cai and others are suspected of committing a crime. A public prosecution was filed. Xu, the prosecutor, stated that the defendant Cai Yunhai, on the 3rd of this month, at 3:00 AM, under the pretext of urinating, took the opportunity to escape by jumping out of the window. The next day, he surrendered himself again. Under investigation, the defendant also confessed, which constituted a crime under Article 170 of the Criminal Law. However, because the defendant surrendered himself afterward, he can reduce the original sentence by one-third according to Article 38 of the Criminal Law. As for Chen Jingcheng, who was in charge of guarding and had important responsibilities, he was unaware that the prisoner had escaped. His dereliction of duty is inexcusable and should be punished according to Article 172 of the Criminal Law. Judge Xu asked Cai Yunhai about the matter, and Cai repeatedly begged for mercy, saying that he had an old mother and children to support, and that his family relied on him for their livelihood. If he was convicted, his elderly mother and young children would lose their support. He pleaded for leniency. Under further cross-examination of Chen Jingcheng, the debate on the case concluded, and the sentencing was scheduled for next Thursday morning.

Page 16

Released from Prison for One Day and Night

Re-arrested for Involvement in a Theft Case

Zhao Zhizhen Has Only Himself to Blame

Zhao Zhizhen, a native of Jiading, was sentenced to three months in prison by the Special District Local Court in June of this year for theft and was sent to the Tilanqiao Prison. He was released on the morning of the 18th of this month after serving his sentence and temporarily resided at 1025 Hede Road. In addition to his wife, Ms. Liu, his fellow villager Shen Liansheng also lived there. However, Zhao was only reunited with his family for one day and night. Suddenly, at 4:00 AM the next day, he was arrested by detectives from the Jing'an Temple Police Station, along with Ms. Liu and Shen. Recently, the Municipal Public Security Bureau arrested a local thief named Lu A'mao. According to Lu's confession, in July of the previous year, he and Zhao, Shen, etc., held weapons and robbed the household of Yangsi Bridge in Pudong. He also stated Zhao's address. The bureau sent detectives Han Ruisheng, etc., to the relevant police station with an official letter, requesting them to dispatch detectives to conduct a surprise arrest before dawn. They were all captured. At 9:00 AM, they were sent to the Special District Court. Detective Han presented the official document and requested a transfer order so that they could be returned to the case for interrogation. Police Barrister Wang Yaotang stated that the police station did not object to the transfer order. However, Zhao confessed that he was framed by enemies, and Shen and Ms. Liu both claimed to be unaware. After questioning, Judge Sun instructed to hand over the three men and women, Zhao Zhizhen, etc., to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

New New Hotel Receptionist

Accuses the Manager and Others of Defaming His Reputation

Fired for Embezzling Public Funds

Actually Making False Accusations Out of Spite

Dai Bangzeng, a receptionist at the New New Company Hotel Department, has been working for many years. In May of this year, the company's manager, Li Minzhou, and associate Chen Yikang discovered that he was using public funds for private purposes and damaging the company's reputation, so they dismissed him. However, Dai did not repent and hired a lawyer to sue Li and Chen for defaming his reputation in the Special District Local Court, requesting that they be punished according to the law. He also filed a private suit demanding compensation for losses of 4,000 yuan. The other morning, Judge Sun Yuan held a hearing. The defendant hired lawyer Chen Tingrui to defend, saying that Dai had embezzled more than 430 yuan, so he was dismissed. Now he is suing for defamation, which is actually an attempt to blackmail. Therefore, the defendant has now decided to file a counterclaim requesting that he be punished for making false accusations. Before the judgment, he must be released on bail. He also submitted a list of the amounts of money that Dai had embezzled. Judge Sun asked the defendant, who admitted to using more than 300 yuan of public funds for private purposes. Judge Sun sternly reprimanded him, saying that since Dai had embezzled, how could he make false accusations out of spite? He then ordered him to pay 1,000 yuan in bail to await the verdict next Saturday.

Meng Ju, a Woman's Divorce Case

The Debate Has Concluded, Waiting for the Judgment

Meng Ju (i.e., Cui Meng'shi), a 39-year-old woman from Dongtai, resides at 144 Miezhu Street, Nanshi. Recently, she hired lawyer Hu Yuanjun to file a lawsuit in the Local Court for divorce. Her statement reads: The plaintiff's fate is unfortunate. In her youth, she was deceived by matchmakers into marrying the defendant Cui Baoqi. However, after she married, the defendant only had a few dilapidated houses, which he soon sold to pay off debts, which were still insufficient. Therefore, he sold all the houses and fields, leaving her with no home to return to. Before long, the plaintiff gave birth to a son and had no choice but to temporarily return to her mother's house to live a hard life. The defendant abandoned her from then on. For many years, the plaintiff and her mother had to come to Shanghai to work and make a living. However, the defendant repeatedly made false accusations in Dongtai County, implicating many people. The plaintiff handed him over to the defendant in court and ordered him not to abandon or abuse her. Unexpectedly, the defendant took the plaintiff to Suzhou and sold her three times. The plaintiff escaped back to her mother's house. Such a husband who has severed all ties, how can she live with him? Therefore, it has been six years since she was sold, and she has not received any news from him. She can only support her son's studies in order to make a living. The defendant saw that the plaintiff's mother had bought a few rickshaws, so he came to harass and seize them again. Since the defendant sold the plaintiff to Suzhou three times and abandoned her for six years, if he is allowed to enter the house and act recklessly again, he will surely squander all of the plaintiff's mother's assets. Therefore, she has no choice but to request that the divorce be granted. Yesterday morning, Judge Guo held a hearing. The defendant's address is unknown, so he could not be served. Lawyer Zhang Enhou was selected to appear in court to defend him. The plaintiff, Meng Ju, submitted a statement recounting the past events and requesting that the divorce be granted. Lawyer Hu also made a statement on her behalf. The judge then declared that the debate had concluded and that the judgment would be announced.

Wu A'tu Died Tragically

Heaved a Long Sigh and Tears Fell Like Rain

The Inside Story is Unknown

Wu A'tu, a local man, 24 years old, lived in the east end of Wu Family Hall, Pudong. He used to work as a substitute sailor on the Li Yongji steamship. He married Ms. So-and-so three years ago, and their relationship was extremely poor. It was rumored that A'tu's brother, A'lin (who worked as an old petrol ship supervisor), had an affair with his sister-in-law. A'tu felt increasingly unwelcome due to this gossip, but because he was weak, he did not dare to clarify the facts directly. Recently, his wife returned to her mother's house for several days. On the 19th, she returned home. The couple stayed together that night. Unexpectedly, the next morning (the day before), the sun was high in the sky, but the two had not yet gotten up. The neighbors were very suspicious and knocked on their door repeatedly. His wife finally opened the door, but her face was ashen and she did not say a word. The neighbors went inside and saw that A'tu was lying on his back on the bed, his face pale. He remained silent and did not make a sound. When someone asked him why he was like this, he heaved a long sigh and tears fell like rain. He still did not answer. Suddenly, a strange sound came from his throat, and his breathing became short. Before long, he died. The onlookers retreated in unison after witnessing this scene. Afterward, they ran around telling each other. Some said that he had committed suicide by swallowing sleeping pills, while others said that the cause of his death was unexpected. Everyone was speculating, and many busybodies went to Wu's house to peek at the dead body, so the inside and outside of the house were crowded. By the evening, no one had yet collected the body. Yesterday, the neighbors advised the deceased's brother, A'lin, to prepare a coffin and collect the body first.

Demolition Dispute in Yongkang Lane

Tenants Discuss Self-Help Measures

Previously, the tenants of Yongkang Lane, North Sichuan Road, received a letter from the landlord's side (Yongkang Company) stating that the houses in the lane had been sold to Wanfu Company and were to be renovated. Therefore, the tenants were ordered to move out by August 15. The tenants found that the company (Yongkang Company) originally had seven shareholders. Now, the Chen and Lu shareholders invested in the acquisition and changed the name to Wanfu Company. They used the excuse of demolition and renovation to drive away the tenants and then made slight repairs so that they could arbitrarily increase the rent (from 16 yuan to 35 yuan). However, these houses were built on land leased from a landlord surnamed Yao in 1913 for a term of twenty years. Subtracting the current time, there are only three years left. When the lease expires, the land must be returned, so it is impossible to demolish the houses. Therefore, the tenants repeatedly negotiated with the landlord, willing to automatically increase the rent, but to no avail. They hired lawyer Chen Wenxiang to file a lawsuit in the Local Court. The court held two hearings that were not concluded and ordered them to reconcile outside the court. Yesterday afternoon, the Yongkang Lane Tenants' Association held a meeting to discuss the matter. Chairman Zheng Guogan reported everything, saying that Judge Zhao Zhenhai of the court had impartially investigated the case and ordered a reconciliation, but the landlord was not sincere about reconciliation and negotiations. Now, they hope that the tenants will remain calm and wait for a legal resolution. The tenants then said that the landlord had ordered the gatekeeper to prevent the cleaners from entering the lane to remove garbage and had cut off the water and electricity and erected bamboo fences, which should be stopped. (1) Committee member She Guinan proposed that the removal of garbage be reported to the Health Bureau. As for the cutting off of water and electricity and the erection of bamboo fences, which are related to public security, they should wait for the landlord to implement them during the litigation period. Besides, the rent has already been deposited in the bank, so the landlord has not suffered any losses. (2) Executive committee member Ouyang Hengran proposed that the landlord secretly requested the Public Works Bureau to issue permits to demolish the front and back doors of the vacant houses, which has led to thefts from neighboring tenants. If any reactionary sneaks into the vacant houses and takes inappropriate actions, the landlord must be held fully responsible. They also proposed to petition the Public Works Bureau to stop issuing permits. The resolution was passed. There were no objections, and the meeting was adjourned.

Commander Xiong Protects the World Theatre

Yesterday, Xiong Shihui, Commander of the Songhu Garrison Command, specially issued a proclamation stating that, according to a report submitted by Bian Yuying, manager of the World Theatre in Zhabei, the theatre had been established for over five years. Although it was a commercial venture funded by merchants, it had contributed in a small way to the prosperity of the Zhabei market. Furthermore, it had achieved early recognition for using the silver screen to promote revolutionary work. As the Chinese people lacked adequate entertainment, the theatre provided a place for relaxation during leisure time. However, due to the recent economic downturn, the theatre's business had declined significantly, causing it substantial losses. Manager Bian Yuying had spared no effort in managing the theatre, but it had been repeatedly harassed by local ruffians and hooligans, falsely claiming to be a small number of lawless military police, acting with extreme barbarity. The theatre had always had preferential treatment for armed comrades, offering half-price tickets. However, incidents of troublemaking often occurred, causing regular patrons to avoid the theatre, which significantly affected its business and had a major impact on local peace and tranquility. The theatre had requested the issuance of a proclamation and the dispatch of a patrol for protection, which temporarily suppressed the disturbances, allowing the theatre to operate in relative peace. Unexpectedly, recently discharged wounded soldiers had arrived, and the theatre staff, sympathetic to their war injuries, offered them extra preferential treatment. As a result, local ruffians seized the opportunity to gather in groups, always arriving in teams. Initially, there were three to five people, some even wearing military uniforms and insignia. Later, they formed groups of forty to fifty, and recently, each time there were nearly a hundred, mostly in plain clothes. They entered without purchasing tickets and then arbitrarily caused trouble. Sometimes, when the theatre asked them to show their passes, they refused, clearly acting as ruffians taking advantage of the military's reputation. Furthermore, they relied on their thuggish behavior to harass female patrons, acting violently and unreasonably. The theatre's premises were small and could not accommodate so many non-paying spectators, and the insult to women was a violation of public morals. For the sake of the theatre's business prospects, this situation had become unbearable, and for the sake of local peace and tranquility, it was even more concerning. Therefore, the theatre had repeatedly submitted requests for the dispatch of a number of troops to protect the theatre during performance times, and for the issuance of a proclamation to strictly prohibit ticketless viewing, so that the military and civilians could coexist peacefully and the theatre's business could continue. It has long been admired that Your Excellency has been stationed in Shanghai for several years, and the discipline of the military has been especially strict, bringing peace to the area, and the theatre has also benefited from it. It is hoped that Your Excellency will give appropriate consideration to the issues of ticketless viewing and the harassment of women, and there will be no limit to the anticipation. Based on this investigation, it is clear that ticketless viewing violates regulations, and arbitrary troublemaking disrupts the law. If this is not strictly prohibited, how can business be maintained and the military's reputation be preserved? Therefore, this proclamation is issued to all subordinate military and police personnel to be aware that, henceforth, when entering the theatre, they must abide by the regulations and must not arbitrarily cause trouble. Anyone who dares to violate this will be severely punished. This proclamation is issued on September 16th of the 19th year of the Republic of China by Xiong Shihui, also the commander. It is also reported that Deputy Adjutant Geng of the 27th Regiment of the 5th Division personally visited the theatre to observe for a week, and Commander Xie has dispatched a platoon of soldiers daily to maintain order in the theatre since the previous day.

As for its rich clothing materials, attentive service, conscientious pricing, and punctual delivery, these are even more trivial.

"All Quiet on the Western Front" Opens to Great Success

"All Quiet on the Western Front," based on German author Erich Maria Remarque's personal experience in the trenches and his witnessed atrocities, was adapted into a film by Universal Pictures. Its premiere caused a sensation in various countries. The film is seventeen reels long and depicts the battlefields. Its cruelty and greatness can be described as unprecedented. It premiered in Shanghai yesterday at the Nanjing Theatre. By 9:00 am, all tickets for the day had been sold out, a grand occasion unprecedented for theaters in Shanghai.

Book and Newspaper Introductions

"The Youth of the Times"

— Tang Bin

Issue 6 Published by Daguang Bookstore

Today's publishing industry in China mostly presents a glaringly poor state of affairs, tending towards commercialization. There is a complete disregard for the introduction of genuinely valuable academic works from around the world and the promotion of Chinese literature. The sole concern is whether or not there will be improvement in their own business. Therefore, the books published focus exclusively on aspects of sex, catering to the psychology and low-level tastes of the general public. Previously, bookstores were filled with distorted and perverted works of art. Recently, many so-called political, social, and scientific books have been published, all of which are sufficient to intoxicate aspiring young people, leading them astray and shaping incorrect thinking. This is not only a crisis for Chinese publishing but also the greatest crisis for Chinese youth. The only way to break through this crisis in the shortest possible time is to start with improving the publications that the average young student of today often encounters. This is the most obvious fact.

Recently, scholars who advocate central thought and nationalistic literature have actively noticed this point. We must understand that the average young person who is currently studying is the pillar of the future China. So we can also say that the rise and fall of the Chinese nation depends on how hard these young people work. However, the will of young people mostly belongs to the weak. The phrase "one who stays near vermilion gets stained red, and one who stays near ink gets stained black" has become an extremely common phenomenon. If we want to make up for this deficiency in will and behavior, we must of course work hard on publications. Because the average young person in school, regardless of whether he has a strange preference for books or not, must at least find some publications to pass the time in his spare time. Sometimes he picks up a pen and writes a few lines of wind and moon, which also influences the so-called distorted and perverted works of art. Other things, such as social sciences, etc., poison young people in the same way. And the bookstores, which only seek the development of their own business, do not pay any attention to the books that help young people solve their own problems. Even if some aspiring young people want to read books about this kind of thing, they have no way to buy them, so they can only go down the distorted road to seek the satisfaction of their literary desires. This is really a pity. It was not until recently that a central publication pointing the way for modern youth came into being. The first thing that is active in front of our eyes is the "The Youth of the Times" weekly magazine, which I now want to piously recommend to the young readers. It has published six issues. The content is very rich and gives us a lot of correct instructions. It has become a good reading material for the average young person in modern China.

The content of this issue is even more exciting. The topics include "The Silence of the Sino-Russian Conference," "The Fall of Young Leaders," "The Future of School Drama Movement," and "The Secret Oath of Jin Guangmei, a Newly Emerging Shanghai Celebrity." Each article is a carefully crafted piece that we must read. They are briefly described separately below.

"The Silence of the Sino-Russian Conference" The author divides the full text into four paragraphs. In the first paragraph, the introduction, the so-called Sino-Russian official conference, which is related to my country's international status, is described in a very concise manner. At the same time, it is mentioned that the Russian side is abusing foreign nations and our Chinese compatriots, so that the average faint young people can understand the fear of the red color. The second paragraph is about the cause of the conference, detailing the incident as if reading a long-term newspaper. Because for a very important event, you must first understand the cause and then examine the success or failure of the result. The author, Mr. Lao, is of course good at writing, so he is very敏捷注意到this. The third paragraph is about the recent situation of the Sino-Russian conference, exposing the aggressive ambitions of Soviet Russia, and discussing it in detail based on correct facts, so that we can understand what kind of situation the Sino-Russian conference is heading towards recently. The fourth paragraph, the concluding remarks, of course summarizes what has been discussed above, but the author, in order to urge the average young people to rise up and strive for this major event, has such a warning at the end: "But young people, we should arouse the enthusiasm in our bodies and strive to glorify the nation, support Mr. Mo, and swear to fight the Soviet Union to the end in order to obtain the glory of our nation's permanent independence."

Drama, a synthesis of the arts, also urgently needs to be promoted in China, where the ideological world is chaotic. At the same time, some incorrect content and theories related to this item in the past need to be explored or corrected, because drama includes hearing and vision in essence, so its effectiveness in the field of art is broader and easier to absorb than other audiences, especially the current students who have a strong love for drama, but they are distorted to seek the satisfaction of desires. The performances in school concerts are nothing more than the song and dance dramas that are still popular in ordinary society today. The performance of this kind of drama is really harmful to Chinese youth, and the "Chinese Students," which is called youth reading, has also published a special issue on school drama movement, but the dramas discussed and introduced in it do not meet the requirements of the average youth, and at the same time instill young people with incorrect ideas. This is really not a sincere attitude to promote drama. From this point of view, the promotion and advocacy of school drama is something that cannot be delayed at present. Mr. Da Zhuang's article "The Future of School Drama Movement" is really worthy of our attention. He discusses the morbid state of old dramas, the mistakes of past drama theories, and the lack of love dramas. In it, he gives detailed development and instructions on the significance and direction of school dramas, such as:

Page 20

Drama stands in a very important position in literature and art. Currently, based on the requirements of the times, nationalistic literary theory has been established in literature and art in order to achieve national survival and evolution. This is what should be done. At a time of suffering, when the nation is invaded and oppressed by foreign races, and its own national consciousness is so depressed, it is bound to rely on the power of literature and art to promote the completion of the political nationalist movement. Now our school drama is aimed solely at young people. In the future, the mission of young people is to bear the responsibility of the nation and the country, to try to restore the inherent youth of this aging and withered nation, and at the same time to nurture and enrich the elements of vitality, and to hope for the prosperity of development. Then, the mission that school drama should bear must only be to promote their strong and consistent national concepts and consciousness, and to fight for national survival.

This is such a painful and precise statement, giving young people a lot of correct instructions. At the same time, scholars who promote school drama with misleading ideas should quickly wake up and not use any poison to anesthetize aspiring young people. At least after reading Mr. Da Zhuang's article.

Guangmei's "Secret Oath" is a short story with profound implications. It describes the various impressions that Mr. and Mrs. Zhang had after watching a film starring Chaplin that humiliated the Chinese nation, and describes it as if the screen were really performing. The various places where our Chinese nation was insulted were very tense and powerful, so that readers could not help but want to jump up. Literary works like this are very much needed at the moment. Mr. Guangmei was able to notice this before us, which is worthy of admiration. The final summary is so compact and powerful, clearly showing the author's talent for writing and creation.

That night, both of them were restless and could not sleep. They sang enthusiastically and generously. They were completely awake. So they stood shoulder to shoulder by the window. He raised his right hand, she raised her left hand, and they swore to the sky: "I, Zhang Zhiwen, and I, Xu Peizhen, from now on, are willing to sacrifice, struggle, and dedicate ourselves to our Chinese nation!" Finally, they shouted in unison.

This is indeed a rare creation with central ideas. It is really worth applauding and rejoicing to be able to meet us on the small "Youth of the Times" weekly magazine. I hope that the "Youth of the Times," which young people must read, will often have such beautiful and powerful creations published after huge treatises, so that we can taste the sour green fruit and taste the delicious chewing gum. How refreshing! I want to say one last word carefully.

"Youth of the Times" is a must-read publication for Chinese youth.

Li Yizhi's arrival in Wuhan (continued), 3. Zhang Jiping's proletarian poems, 4. Jin Xuan's talk show, 5. Zheng Bo's translation of "Two Orphans" (continued). Youth Garden

The "Tai Meng" Western Painting Research Society

In recent years, the art movement in our country has been very prosperous, but in terms of quality, although it is developing day by day, in terms of quantity, there is very little strength. The reason is that there are no purely art research institutions other than schools. The Tai Meng Painting Society, in view of this, has specially invited famous artists from home and abroad to establish a research institute, so that art lovers can have more opportunities for research and cultivate advanced art. The association has now published advertisements soliciting researchers. The content equipment is similar to the Académie in Paris, France. Everything is quite perfect. Western painters such as Hu Daozhi, Pang Xunqin, Wang Dilang, Zhou Tai, Guo Gu, Niliu Yanren, etc. are in charge of guidance. Practical training has already begun.

On Qinglong Bridge

— Wen Juan

The golden wind shatters the sky, bringing autumn. Teachers and students from schools, seeking to gather materials, also take this opportunity to travel to mountain peaks and riverbanks to collect specimens. Our group discussed going to Qinglong Bridge, because it is the highest point on the Jing-Sui Railway, on the northern side of the Great Wall. There should be plenty of flowers, plants, and insects to find there. On a clear, blue Sunday morning, we set off. On the train from Xuanhua to Qinglong Bridge, a large flag of the provincial No. XX middle school fluttered in the wind, seeming to act as a pioneer for us. After passing through several tunnels, and gazing at the Great Wall, like a chain locking the great and solemn Badaling mountain range, it appeared distinctly before our eyes. The students, lively and jostling, got off the train, each carrying their specimen boxes and food boxes. Some had their hands free, with only a camera slung over their shoulders, or a diary tucked under their arms, as they leisurely left the station and followed the road towards the Great Wall.

Midway, we encountered many foreign ladies sitting anxiously in bamboo chairs, carried up and down by two sedan chair bearers. I saw that they showed surprised expressions towards our group of lively and jumping female students who were not afraid of the long and winding stone paths, perhaps thinking we were admirable women of the new China, or perhaps thinking we were lowly girls who didn't deserve to ride in sedan chairs. Whether they cursed us or praised us, it was none of our business. We, these twenty or thirty people unafraid of hardship and danger, had already climbed to the top and were standing on the ramparts, singing travel songs.

Xin advocated taking deep breaths. Everyone echoed her. For a moment, the sound of laughter and chatter ceased, with only the light sound of arms swinging spreading in the west wind.

"I found a golden bellflower!"

"I saw a wild man's blood plant!"

"Hey, there's a jade beetle here!"

"Don't be noisy, you'll scare away my tricolored butterfly!"

These whispers filled the still valleys of the Great Wall, like music heard in a dream, fleeting and mysterious. I, however, did not move, but stared entranced at the overlapping mountain peaks and the rivers, small as ribbons. The water flowed, weaving around the foothills, the railway weaving around the riverbanks, extending endlessly into the distance. A touch of green mountain was entangled by the white Great Wall, seeming to end only at the edge of the sky. White clouds brushed across the sky like upside-down phoenix tails. The autumn scenery was already beautiful enough, and even more so in such surroundings.

"Are you daydreaming?" Qing forcefully pulled at the corner of my skirt. It turned out that she was sitting on the ground digging up the root of a grass. This was a kind of Asteraceae plant, commonly called "fire lala," which is not easy to find in the north, so Qing was working so hard. I saw that she didn't use a shovel but used her ten fingers as tools and had almost dug out the main root, her hands covered in mud, not caring about the dirt.

"Why don't you use a small knife?"

"Hmph, what do you know? If I use a knife, the fine roots will be cut off."

Soon, the students scattered in various places all returned.

Just now, it was empty valleys; now, it's a triumphant return. With a roar, everyone laughed. Then, they sat down on the ground, took out the food boxes they had brought, placed them on a rock, and prepared to eat and drink. Everyone was busy grabbing and tearing at chicken legs.

"This group of famine refugees must not have eaten for three years, right?"

Someone said this and grabbed four steamed buns and walked away to eat them. In a flash, a whirlwind swept through, and fifteen or sixteen food boxes and several baskets of steamed buns were already empty. I felt that since I learned to eat, I had never had such a delicious meal as that day. The good mountain air must be a reason for increasing appetite.

The faint sun shone on the tired faces of the people after their full meal. Everyone seemed a little sleepy. Mr. Zhang, wearing yellow riding clothes and holding a small wooden box, also hurried over from a distant mountain. Her face was covered in sweat, and she was panting like a goat that had just been chased by a tiger, shouting in her mouth:

"Terrible, terrible! You all go and take a look!"

We were awakened by her shouting, and we all cheered up and listened to her report. She put down the box, wiped the sweat from her face, and slowly said:

"There's a big wolf lying in a cave over there!"

Everyone wanted to act like heroes, vying to say, "I'll go first!" Even Ping, who had never dared to step on a cockroach, said she wasn't afraid. The result was ten people formed a team, for a total of two and a half teams. Mr. Zhang was the captain, and the team headed mightily towards the back of the mountain. Each person perked up their spirits, carried the camera tripod as a charging weapon, and used the pillow box as an attack tool, aiming it at the place indicated by Mr. Zhang, looking towards it.

Only a long howl was heard, and in an instant, the mountains and valleys echoed, and the yellow leaves in the forest rustled, falling with the wind, making strange sounds. Ping tightly grasped my clothes, her body crouched down more than halfway. Some retreated, and some hid secretly, taking advantage of the ambush.

"In the trap! In the net!"

Someone discovered it first and shouted. Then, everyone's courage was restored all at once. Those hidden elsewhere also came out, peeking to see if this yellow wolf that had already been caught could still come out and eat people. Fortunately, a hunter had already jumped out from behind a tree, locked the lid of the wire cage, and carried it on his back as if to go home. Mr. Zhang asked him for two wolf teeth. The hunter agreed to send them over in a while and happily went down the mountain with his trophy.

We also sighed in relief, as if we had also contributed to this victory.

Mother and Child

— Photographed by Su Duyu

We started searching for objects again, hoping that we could be so lucky and get something safely. All kinds of wild grasses filled everyone's boxes. The flying and crawling insects lay lazily in glass-covered boxes.

Today's harvest was quite good, except that Mr. Zhang's wolf teeth seemed to be obtained too easily.

I think that when we re-embarked on our return journey, the sun had already hidden its face, leaving only its departing autumn waves, faintly shining on the verdant mountain tops for a moment towards the human world. We stepped on this ancient road in the setting sun, looking back at the towering Great Wall, standing alone like the shadow of a giant, disappearing into the vast twilight.
